# Skyrim:Clan Shatter-Shield Office

## Overview

|  |  |  |

Interior of Clan Shatter-Shield Office

**Clan Shatter-Shield Office** is a small office in [Windhelm](/wiki/Skyrim:Windhelm "Skyrim:Windhelm") that is home to Clan Shatter-Shield's shipping operations.

The office is located on Windhelm's docks, between the [Argonian Assemblage](/wiki/Skyrim:Argonian_Assemblage "Skyrim:Argonian Assemblage") and the [East Empire Company regional office](/wiki/Skyrim:East_Empire_Company_(place) "Skyrim:East Empire Company (place)"). It contains one interior zone: *[Clan Shatter-Shield Office](#Clan_Shatter-Shield_Office)*.

## Related Quests

- **[Rise in the East](/wiki/Skyrim:Rise_in_the_East "Skyrim:Rise in the East")**: Help the [East Empire Company](/wiki/Lore:East_Empire_Company "Lore:East Empire Company") take care of some [pirates](/wiki/Skyrim:Blood_Horker "Skyrim:Blood Horker").

## Clan Shatter-Shield Office

The building is a busy shipping hub run by the Shatter-Shields' employee, [Suvaris Atheron](/wiki/Skyrim:Suvaris_Atheron "Skyrim:Suvaris Atheron"). There is a long wooden table and three chairs holding a copy of *[Thief of Virtue](/wiki/Skyrim:Thief_of_Virtue "Skyrim:Thief of Virtue")* right in front of the entrance, with several empty carts to the east and west. The middle section is full of crates, and the rear section has a small wooden table and chair to the west, with the [business ledger](/wiki/Skyrim:Business_Ledger "Skyrim:Business Ledger"), a level-locked non-respawning [strongbox](/wiki/Skyrim:Strongbox "Skyrim:Strongbox") containing random items, a bottle of [Nord mead](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord_Mead "Skyrim:Nord Mead"), a small [coin purse](/wiki/Skyrim:Coin_Purse "Skyrim:Coin Purse"), and an important clue required for the relevant [quest](/wiki/Skyrim:Rise_in_the_East "Skyrim:Rise in the East") - [Suvaris's logbook](/wiki/Skyrim:Suvaris_Atheron%27s_Logbook "Skyrim:Suvaris Atheron's Logbook") - on the table. An unlocked respawning empty [chest](/wiki/Skyrim:Chest "Skyrim:Chest") is to the east, and to the north is a set of shelves directly opposite the entrance holding copies of *[Of Fjori and Holgeir](/wiki/Skyrim:Of_Fjori_and_Holgeir "Skyrim:Of Fjori and Holgeir")* (see [notes](#Notes)), *[Beggar Prince](/wiki/Skyrim:Beggar_Prince "Skyrim:Beggar Prince")*, *[Antecedants of Dwemer Law](/wiki/Skyrim:Antecedants_of_Dwemer_Law "Skyrim:Antecedants of Dwemer Law")*, *[Report: Disaster at Ionith](/wiki/Skyrim:Report:_Disaster_at_Ionith "Skyrim:Report: Disaster at Ionith")*, and *[The Wolf Queen, v5](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Wolf_Queen,_v5 "Skyrim:The Wolf Queen, v5")*, as well as a bottle of [alto wine](/wiki/Skyrim:Alto_Wine "Skyrim:Alto Wine"), with a large pile of [food](/wiki/Skyrim:Food "Skyrim:Food") sacks on and in front of the shelves.

## Notes

- The book *Of Fjori and Holgeir* relates to the quest [Ansilvund](/wiki/Skyrim:Ansilvund_(quest) "Skyrim:Ansilvund (quest)").
- None of the sacks in the office are [respawning](/wiki/Skyrim:Respawning "Skyrim:Respawning"), so they are safe to store items in.

# Skyrim:Classes

## Overview

In Skyrim, a **class** cannot be chosen by the player character, but is instead used by [NPCs](/wiki/Skyrim:NPCs "Skyrim:NPCs"). There may be some classes that appear identical to each other. The difference between such classes are the [services](/wiki/Skyrim:Services "Skyrim:Services") offered, which are not listed here.

## Skill and Attribute Weights

The numbers in the table are the weights assigned by the classes to each [skill](/wiki/Skyrim:Skills "Skyrim:Skills") and each [attribute](/wiki/Skyrim:Attributes "Skyrim:Attributes") (empty cells have a weight of zero). These weights determine how many of 8 skill points and 10 attribute points per level are added to each value. Note that 5 points per gained level are always added to [Health](/wiki/Skyrim:Health "Skyrim:Health"), *in addition to* any health points from the shared set of 10 attribute points; this means NPCs gain 15 attributes per level, in addition to *approximately* 8 skill points per level (see below).

Unlike the PC, there is no intrinsic mechanism for an NPC to gain *perks* as they level; a stock leveled NPC has the same perks at any level. This is one of the reasons [leveled lists](/wiki/Skyrim:Leveled_Lists "Skyrim:Leveled Lists") exist. For example, a [Bandit](/wiki/Skyrim:Bandit "Skyrim:Bandit") Thug and a Bandit Highwayman are fundamentally the same NPC at levels 9 and 14, respectively (they are both members of the Bandit Archer class, below), but the former has the [Extra Damage 1.5](/wiki/Skyrim:Extra_Damage_1.5 "Skyrim:Extra Damage 1.5") perk, while the latter has [Extra Damage 2](/wiki/Skyrim:Extra_Damage_2 "Skyrim:Extra Damage 2"). Because perks are manually assigned to an NPC independently of its level or class (and hence independently of its skill expertise and attributes), mismatches exist; this is particularly noticeable among [followers](/wiki/Skyrim:Followers "Skyrim:Followers").

Class and perks are also not automatically tied to equipment or spells in any way, leading to the same mismatches; while the aforementioned Thug and Highwayman share the same leveled lists for equipment, and their level is used to determine what they have, these lists were assigned manually, not by the class (or [race](/wiki/Skyrim:Races "Skyrim:Races")). Typically, these mismatches are less obviously unintentional, particularly when an NPC lacks *any* equipment, but still sometimes leads to followers carrying weapons they do not know how to use.

### Attribute Weights

The game ensures attribute points are not lost or gained due to rounding, but it is easy for an NPC's number of attribute points to not be an integer multiple of a weight (for example, Imperial Soldiers have a Stamina weight of 7, but can be level 37). Attribute points are actually assigned as follows:

1. Calculate the total number of points available (10 \* (level - 1))
2. Calculate the result for the attribute with the highest weight, rounded down, and subtract that from the total.
   - In the event of a tie, choose Health over Magicka or Stamina, and Magicka over Stamina.
3. Repeat for the next-highest result, remembering to use the ratio of only the two remaining attributes.
4. Any remaining points go to the last attribute.

This means there is a weighting bias in favor of Stamina over Magicka and Magicka over Health, because Stamina is intrinsically chosen last and gets anything the others lost due to rounding, but Health gets 1/3 of each level's attribute points before assignment. For example:

- A beggar has weights 1, 1, 1 - all equal. A beggar at level 8 (70 attribute points, plus 35 mandatory health points) calculates as follows:
  1. Health is assigned 23 points (70/3, rounded down), then adds 35: Health +58.
  2. Magicka is assigned 23 points ((70-23)/2, rounded down): Magicka +23.
  3. Stamina is assigned 24 points (70-23-23): Stamina +24.

### Skill Weights

In the "Primary Skills" summary on individual NPC pages, skills with values of 3 or greater are normally emphasized in **bold** face, skills with a value of 2 are shown in normal font, and skills with a value of 1 or 0 are not listed. However, on NPCs with a fixed low level, the displayed skills are adjusted taking into account racial skill bonuses, with only skills greater than 25 being shown.

Unlike with Attributes, an NPC is capable of "losing" or "gaining" skill points due to rounding; a skill gains skill points in accordance with:

```
This Skill Points = round(Total Skill Points * (This Skill Weight / Sum of Skill Weights))
```

Where Total Skill Points = (Level-1)\*8; an NPC's skill points at level 1 are 15 (a game-wide constant) base, then modified by its race.

Note the *drastic* difference between NPCs and the PC: for the PC, each [level](/wiki/Skyrim:Leveling "Skyrim:Leveling") takes more skill ranks than the level before did, while NPCs gain a linear (aside from rounding errors) number of skill points per level. On the other hand, the PC needs less than 8 skill points to level initially (only 4 are needed in the skill the PC's race is best at to level) and that number depends on which skill is being leveled (since the 100th rank in a skill counts for more than the 16th); assuming the PC is leveling as quickly as possible, their skill ranks per level will only *exceed* 8 (meaning the NPCs have begun "winning") at level 33.

Because NPCs face the same skill maximum of 100 ranks as the PC, however, and unlike the PC, will *not* resort to putting skill points into non-preferential (0 weight, below) skills - the formula above *always* holds true - past a certain point, which depends on the NPC's class, they will cease to gain *any* skill points per level, and will only gain attributes. An excellent example of this is [Arngeir](/wiki/Skyrim:Arngeir "Skyrim:Arngeir"), who is level 150, but stopped gaining skill points at level 139 (which is when he reached 100 ranks in Enchanting). In addition, none of his leveled skills *do* anything - he has no weapons or armor to smith or enchant (nor would he, if he did have them - NPCs with crafting skills do not automatically craft anything), no potions indicative of his alchemy, no spells to cast with conjuration or restoration (he only has shouts), and no way to use the speech skill. This is indicative of how the game usually works - there is simply no framework in place allowing NPCs to "automatically" employ their skills, so it has to be assigned manually. This is why you routinely see NPCs like Arngeir, with magic skills but no spells to cast with them, crafting skills but nothing crafted to show for it (which is why the PC is the only source of smithed gear in the game - NPCs *never* carry Fine or better gear), speech without relatively increased money or gear quality (as is found on the PC), etc.

#### Mismatch Examples

As the table below shows, many physical-combat-oriented classes such as [Stormcloak](/wiki/Skyrim:Stormcloaks "Skyrim:Stormcloaks") ("Sons of Skyrim") Guards and Soldiers (Class IDs `GuardSonsSkyrim` and `SoldierSonsSkyrimNotGuard` respectively) and [Orc](/wiki/Skyrim:Orc "Skyrim:Orc") Warriors (`GuardOrc1H` and `GuardOrc2H`) have no magic skills, yet are weighted toward [Magicka](/wiki/Skyrim:Magicka "Skyrim:Magicka") as well as [Health](/wiki/Skyrim:Health "Skyrim:Health") as their levels increase, leaving them with stunted [Stamina](/wiki/Skyrim:Stamina "Skyrim:Stamina"). Consequently, if you keep them in melee range but avoid or [Block](/wiki/Skyrim:Block "Skyrim:Block") (or simply withstand) their swings, they rapidly become less dangerous than they should be, from exhaustion. They are also an unexpectedly good source of unused Magicka to [Absorb](/wiki/Skyrim:Absorb_Magicka "Skyrim:Absorb Magicka") from them during the fight.

Numerous NPCs likewise come with gear that is not suited at all to their specializations (e.g. [Light Armor](/wiki/Skyrim:Light_Armor "Skyrim:Light Armor") when they should have [Heavy](/wiki/Skyrim:Heavy_Armor "Skyrim:Heavy Armor"), or [One-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:One-handed "Skyrim:One-handed") weapons when they should have [Two-handed](/wiki/Skyrim:Two-handed "Skyrim:Two-handed")). If gear they should prefer is dropped near them, they will not pick it up and switch. Even using the [Console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to give them armor they should like will not make them auto-equip any of it in most cases, due to the game's pre-set Outfits system; they typically must be forced to equip it with `EquipItem <BaseID>`. (This does not apply to long-term followers, who provide inventory access, though you sometimes have to take things away from them to get them to use what you want.)

A more specific example of how the lack of automatic perks and gear can lead to apparent absurdity is provided by the three [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard") followers that have no maximum level: [Celann](/wiki/Skyrim:Celann "Skyrim:Celann"), [Durak](/wiki/Skyrim:Durak "Skyrim:Durak"), and [Ingjard](/wiki/Skyrim:Ingjard "Skyrim:Ingjard"), particularly without the [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch").

Ingjard has no perks at all, but is a [Nord](/wiki/Skyrim:Nord "Skyrim:Nord") `CombatWarrior2H`, meaning she reaches 100 skill in Two-handed very quickly (at level 36), then stops getting any better at it. [Celann](/wiki/Skyrim:Celann "Skyrim:Celann") is a [Breton](/wiki/Skyrim:Breton "Skyrim:Breton") `CombatWarrior1H`, meaning he reaches 100 in the same skill *much* slower (level 118), but he has the [Extra Damage 1.5](/wiki/Skyrim:Extra_Damage_1.5 "Skyrim:Extra Damage 1.5") perk, meaning he will do the same damage as Ingjard once he reaches skill 80 at level 90, and then continue on to surpass her; in addition, he inexplicably has [Champion's Stance](/wiki/Skyrim:Champion%27s_Stance "Skyrim:Champion's Stance"), letting him power attack more often than she does right from the start, with the same Two-handed weapons he does not have any skill with yet.

Meanwhile, both Celann and Durak have [Custom Fit](/wiki/Skyrim:Custom_Fit "Skyrim:Custom Fit"), even though Celann has *zero* skill weight on Light Armor (Durak does have skill weight on Light Armor); *both* wear Light Armor stock, so Durak will be drastically more durable if you do not issue Celann new gear, and even if you do give him some heavy armor, he will be at a constant disadvantage.

None of the three has access to any sort of leveled lists for gear, so they will carry the same gear at any level unless you give them something better to carry.

# Skyrim:Clavicus Vile

## Overview

The Shrine of Clavicus Vile

**Clavicus Vile** is the [Daedric Prince](/wiki/Lore:Daedric_Princes "Lore:Daedric Princes") of wishes, typically depicted as a small, jovial man with horns protruding from his head. His companion, [Barbas](/wiki/Skyrim:Barbas "Skyrim:Barbas"), is usually shown as a dog, but his form can vary; in Skyrim, Barbas is present in his dog form.

Clavicus Vile's shrine in Skyrim is located at the end of [Haemar's Shame](/wiki/Skyrim:Haemar%27s_Shame "Skyrim:Haemar's Shame"), a cavern that is home to vampires that worship him. Vile's statue shows him holding his artifact, the [Masque of Clavicus Vile](/wiki/Skyrim:Masque_of_Clavicus_Vile "Skyrim:Masque of Clavicus Vile"). At the beginning of the [related quest](/wiki/Skyrim:A_Daedra%27s_Best_Friend "Skyrim:A Daedra's Best Friend"), Barbas will be absent from the statue due to taking on a living form. The choices made during the quest determine whether or not Barbas returns to his master's side.

Barbas offers much information about Clavicus Vile, both on his strength and their connection: *"My master and I had a bit of a falling out. We got into an argument and it got rather... heated. He's kicked me out until I find someone who can settle our disagreement. That's where you come in."* If you agree to help him out, he will reply, *"Thank you. Now, since he banished me, Vile's been rather weak. He can't manifest very far from one of his shrines."* The Daedric Prince later confirms this himself. Clavicus Vile is also not always keen on keeping the deals he makes.

Despite his power being linked to Barbas, Clavicus Vile is certainly not fond of him, willing to not only banish him from the shrine but to order his death, something that not even Barbas expected. He appears to be fond of creating new twists on the deals he makes, saying that *"I'd simply snap my fingers, and everyone in Skyrim would die. War resolved.*" if you ask him to put an end to the civil war. Another instance of this happened much earlier to a man named [Sebastian Lort](/wiki/Skyrim:Sebastian_Lort "Skyrim:Sebastian Lort"), who wished for a cure for his daughter's [lycanthropy](/wiki/Skyrim:Werewolf "Skyrim:Werewolf") and was given [the Rueful Axe](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Rueful_Axe "Skyrim:The Rueful Axe") in response.

## Related Quests

- **[A Daedra's Best Friend](/wiki/Skyrim:A_Daedra%27s_Best_Friend "Skyrim:A Daedra's Best Friend")**: Help [Barbas](/wiki/Skyrim:Barbas "Skyrim:Barbas") reunite with his [master](/wiki/Lore:Clavicus_Vile "Lore:Clavicus Vile").

## Quest-Related Events

Once you've slain the vampires, approach the shrine:

:   **Lord Vile, I have a request of you.**
:   *"By all means, let's hear it. It's the least I could do, since you already helped me grant one final wish for my last worshippers... They were suffering so from vampirism, and begged me for a cure. Then you came and ended their misery! I couldn't have planned it better myself. So, what's your heart's desire? What kind of deal can we strike?"*

You have three possible answers in total:

:   **I'm just here to reunite you with Barbas.**
:   *"Ugh. That insufferable pup? Forget it. Request denied. No deal. I'm glad to be rid of him. Even if it does mean I'm stuck in this pitiful shrine, in the back end of... nowhere. Well... perhaps there is a way he could earn his place back at my side. Maybe. But no promises."*

:   **An end to the civil war that plagues my land.**
:   *"Oh, if I had my full power, granting that would be trivial. I'd simply snap my fingers, and everyone in Skyrim would die. War resolved."*
:   **The power to crush all before me!**

:   *"Really? Power? Haven't you already killed enough of your foes using the more mundane means at your disposal? Swords, magic, etc.? How... uninspired."* (if [Dragon Rising](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Rising "Skyrim:Dragon Rising") has not been completed)
:   **OR** *"Really? Power? You're a dragonborn; you already have more power than most people who aren't immense, fire-breathing monsters."* (if Dragon Rising has been completed)

Additionally, choosing the last two options will have him continue:

:   *"As much as I hate to say it, you're almost as powerful as I am right now. But that's just because half of my power resides in that mutt, Barbas. Come to think of it, I know of a win-win situation for both of us."*

Whichever option you chose you can now ask him what the offer is:

:   **What's your offer?**
:   *"There's an axe. An incredibly powerful axe. An axe powerful enough for me to have quite a bit of fun, indeed. If you bring it to me, I'll grant you my boon. No strings attached. No messy surprises. At least, not for you. As I recall, it's resting in Rimerock Burrow. Barbas can lead you right to it. The little mutt might even earn his place back at my side."*

If asked again:

:   **What did you want, again?**
:   *"In Rimerock Burrow, there's an artifact called the Rueful Axe. Bring it to me, and I'll take Barbas back. Simple as that."*

Once you're back with the Rueful Axe, he will be pleased to see you:

:   *"Ah, you've got the axe! And my dog. Splendid."*
:   **We're back. Now fulfill your end of the bargain.**
:   *"Excellent work. A hero and his faithful companion, retrieving the ancient artifact for the prince. It's almost... storybook. Ah, but it almost seems a shame to give a weapon like that away, doesn't it? I suppose I could be persuaded to let you keep it... But only if you use the axe to kill Barbas. Simple as that."*

You can either agree or refuse:

:   **I sure would like to keep this axe...**
:   *"And I could absorb the spirit of poor, dead Barbas. He'd still be reunited with me. And I'm sure Barbas doesn't want me to have that axe. He'd want it this way. The choice is yours, friend. We're all counting on you to make the right decision. Put him out of our misery!"*

:   **No deal. Take the axe and take back Barbas!**
:   *"Hrmph. You're no fun at all. Guess I'll have to make my own fun elsewhere. And with the pup back, I'll be restored to my full power. There's a whole world just waiting for me!"*

Barbas will interject, saying, *"Wait a second, there's another option here."* If asked, he will speak of an alternate reward for refusing: the Masque of Clavicus Vile. You can also walk away to think it over first, and telling Clavicus this will have him ask, *"And?"* Either way, you have to choose between killing Barbas or sparing him. If you state that you'll keep the axe, you can still change your mind and spare Barbas. However, you cannot reverse your decision if you hand the axe over.

If you kill Barbas, ask Clavicus if you're done here. He will seem satisfied with the outcome: *"Absolutely! Now I can reabsorb his body, and return to full power. All without having to listen to his whining. Oh, sure, he'll be back in a century or two, but think of the fun I can have 'til then."* He'll wish you to *"Enjoy that axe! And don't worry about poor old Barbas. After all, he really should have picked a better friend..."*, his voice disappearing afterwards.

If Barbas lives, the two of them will instead have a brief exchange:

Barbas reuinted with his master

**Barbas**: *"I knew I could trust you!"*
**Clavicus**: *"Yeah, yeah, dog gets master, master gets cosmic axe, everyone's happy. Just get over here, mutt."*
**Barbas**: *"Don't worry. I'll make sure he sees the light. I trusted you, now you trust me."*

As Barbas turns into stone, Clavicus will then remark, *"Ah, that feels so much better! You forget how nice supreme power feels until you've been stuck in a cave for a few years."* What he says after depends on your dialogue earlier: if you only wanted to reunite him and Barbas, he will continue, *"It's a shame you wished for something so dull as me taking back the mutt. Quite the lack of imagination on your part. A lack of ambition like that really ought to be punished. Perhaps by turning you into a worm, or maybe a few decades of..."* If your wish was for the civil war to end, he will instead say, *"Now, as for your wish... An end to the war, was it? I'll make sure this war ends, all right. Just as soon as the dragons swarm across Skyrim and wipe out all of you puny..."* Alternatively, if you wished for power, he will tell you, *"Now, as for your wish... Power, was it? You can be a part of a tremendous power - all you have to do is let your soul be absorbed by this axe. I never said it would be your power..."* Either way, he will fortunately change his mind, dismissing you with *"Oh, fine. Have my boon and be done with it. Got more interesting deals to make, anyway."* and leaving you with the Masque of Clavicus Vile.

## Notes

- Some of his dialogue is unused:
  - Before you set out to retrieve the Rueful Axe, he would have said, *"Collect the Rueful Axe from Rimerock Burrow, and I believe we'll have a deal."*
  - If Barbas is dead, he would have commented, *"It's nice to be rid of that detestable dog. Things are so much more fun without his incessant preaching."*
  - His other greetings include *"Ah, there you are. I've been waiting for you to arrive."* and *"You have business with Clavicus Vile?"*
  - If Barbas lives, Clavicus would have said, *"And I was so close to being rid of you."* Later on, you could have activated his shrine to comment, **"I see he's having a good influence on you."** and he would have replied in frustration: *"Yeah, rub it in. Just imagine what I could get done with my full power and none of these pesky 'morals.' Still, I've got this axe, and even if I can't use it, I'm sure someone would make a deal for it. Maybe I'll have a word with [Molag Bal](/wiki/Lore:Molag_Bal "Lore:Molag Bal")..."* However, activating his shrine after the quest does nothing.
- Another aspect of Clavicus Vile, [Umbra](/wiki/Skyrim:Umbra_(person) "Skyrim:Umbra (person)"), appears in the [Umbra](/wiki/Skyrim:Umbra "Skyrim:Umbra") [Creation](/wiki/Skyrim:Creation_Club "Skyrim:Creation Club") together with the [sword](/wiki/Skyrim:Umbra_(item) "Skyrim:Umbra (item)") of the same name.

An ash spawn emerging from an ash pit

## Quick Walkthrough

1. Speak to [Elder Othreloth](/wiki/Skyrim:Elder_Othreloth "Skyrim:Elder Othreloth") at [Raven Rock Temple](/wiki/Skyrim:Temple "Skyrim:Temple").
2. Clear the [Temple Ancestral Tomb](/wiki/Skyrim:Temple_Ancestral_Tomb "Skyrim:Temple Ancestral Tomb") of [ash spawn](/wiki/Skyrim:Ash_Spawn "Skyrim:Ash Spawn").
3. Return to Othreloth.

### Elder Othreloth

In the [Temple](/wiki/Skyrim:Temple "Skyrim:Temple") of [Raven Rock](/wiki/Skyrim:Raven_Rock "Skyrim:Raven Rock"), the residing priest [Elder Othreloth](/wiki/Skyrim:Elder_Othreloth "Skyrim:Elder Othreloth") has a huge problem with the [Ancestral Tomb](/wiki/Skyrim:Temple_Ancestral_Tomb "Skyrim:Temple Ancestral Tomb") underneath the temple. While patrolling around Raven Rock between 1pm and 7pm, Second Councilor [Adril Arano](/wiki/Skyrim:Adril_Arano "Skyrim:Adril Arano") may visit the chapel and receive yet another complaint by the troubled priest:

*"When are you going to do something about our central Ancestral Tomb?"*

**Adril**: *"You wanted to speak to me, Elder?"*
**Othreloth**: *"I did indeed. When are you going to do something about our central Ancestral Tomb? I can't even go down there any longer. It's getting intolerable!"*
**Adril**: *"I'm sorry, Elder. I'm doing the best I can."*
**Othreloth**: *"I appreciate your problems, Adril, but I can't be expected to run a temple with those... things running around in there."*
**Adril**: *"With all due respect, those "things" aren't the only problem we have right now. Be patient, keep the door locked, and we'll get there when we can."*
**Othreloth**: *"Hmph. Very well. I'll just have to find someone else to assist us then."*

With the authorities too busy to help him out, Elder Othreloth will have no choice but to lure adventurers like you to help him. When he sees you he will ask: *"Are you here to pray, or perhaps pay your respects at our Ancestral Tomb?"* When you ask him what the tomb is, he will immediately request some assistance and provide some background information in the process: *"They are where we inter our dead. They are sacred places, meant to honor their passing. Sadly, we've been unable to use the Ancestral Tomb beneath the Temple as of late, and have resorted to other locations to scatter the remains."* He will then proceed to explain that [ash spawn](/wiki/Skyrim:Ash_Spawn "Skyrim:Ash Spawn") have taken over the tomb, making it impossible to perform proper burial rituals. Offer to help him out and he will hand you the [key](/wiki/Skyrim:Raven_Rock_Tomb_Key "Skyrim:Raven Rock Tomb Key") to the tomb and wish you the best of luck.

### Cleanse the Tomb

Head downstairs and unlock the door to the tomb with the key. Once inside, the problem soon manifests itself, as a total of eleven hostile ash spawn will crawl out of the various huge ceremonial urns with the ashes of the ancestors. They will surface one by one at first, then two at a time. While most will be regular ash spawn, two of those that spawn near the end are leveled.

Dispose of them all as quickly as possible, because they can easily gang up on you. If necessary, exit the tomb through any of the doors to restore your health; the ash spawn cannot follow you. Lower-level players will find the [Become Ethereal](/wiki/Skyrim:Become_Ethereal "Skyrim:Become Ethereal") shout useful to avoid damage when carrying out hit-and-run attacks.

When all is said and done, loot the ash piles as they have a chance of carrying valuable loot, then leave the tomb and return to Othreloth. When presented with the good news, Othreloth will exclaim: *"Spirits be praised! I'm hoping you didn't suffer much at the hands of those foul beings. Please, accept this as a token of my thanks."* He will then hand you a reward, a leveled amount of gold.

### Reward

| Levels | Reward |
| --- | --- |
| 1-29 | 250 |
| 30-39 | 500 |
| 40-49 | 1000 |
| 50-59 | 1500 |
| 60+ | 2000 |

## Quest Stages

| --- | --- | --- |
| Stage | Finishes Quest | Journal Entry |
| 20 |  | *Objective 10:* Clear the Temple's tomb of ash spawn |
| 30 |  | *Objective 20:* Tell Elder Othreloth that the Tomb has been cleansed |

- The following empty quest stages were omitted from the table: 10, 200, 250.

Notes

- Any text displayed in angle brackets (e.g., `<Alias=LocationHold>`) is dynamically set by the Radiant Quest system, and will be filled in with the appropriate word(s) when seen in game.
- Not all Journal Entries may appear in your journal; which entries appear and which entries do not depends on the manner in which the quest is done.
- Stages are not always in order of progress. This is usually the case with quests that have multiple possible outcomes or quests where certain tasks may be done in any order. Some stages may therefore repeat objectives seen in other stages.
- If an entry is marked as "Finishes Quest" it means the quest disappears from the Active Quest list, but you may still receive new entries for that quest.
- On the PC, it is possible to use the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to advance through the quest by entering `setstage DLC2RRFavor03 stage`, where `stage` is the number of the stage you wish to complete. It is not possible to un-complete (i.e. go back) quest stages, but it is possible to clear all stages of the quest using `resetquest DLC2RRFavor03`.

# Skyrim:Cleansing Light

## Overview

|  |
| --- |
| **This page is currently being rewritten as part of the [Skyrim Quest Redesign Project](/wiki/UESPWiki:Skyrim_Quest_Redesign_Project "UESPWiki:Skyrim Quest Redesign Project").** The page is being rewritten and checked in several stages. All users are welcome to make changes to the page. If you make a change that is relevant to the project, please update this template accordingly, and make sure you have observed the [project guidelines](/wiki/UESPWiki:Skyrim_Quest_Redesign_Project#Guidelines "UESPWiki:Skyrim Quest Redesign Project").  Details  **Walkthrough**: written by [SerCenKing](/wiki/User:SerCenKing "User:SerCenKing"), *not checked*  **Reward**: written by [Kimi the Elf](/wiki/User:Kimi_the_Elf "User:Kimi the Elf"), checked by [SerCenKing](/wiki/User:SerCenKing "User:SerCenKing") |

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| [SR-qico-Dawnguard Dawnguard.png](/wiki/File:SR-qico-Dawnguard_Dawnguard.png) | **Kill the boss of a [vampire](/wiki/Skyrim:Vampire "Skyrim:Vampire") lair.** |

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Quest Giver: | [Gunmar](/wiki/Skyrim:Gunmar "Skyrim:Gunmar") |
| Location(s): | Radiant [vampire lair](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Vampire_Lairs "Category:Skyrim-Places-Vampire Lairs") |
| Reward: | Leveled enchanted item |
| ID: | DLC1RH02 |

*"Destroying the head vampire is usually sufficient to scatter its minions..."*

## Quick Walkthrough

1. Speak with [Gunmar](/wiki/Skyrim:Gunmar "Skyrim:Gunmar").
2. Kill the boss at the [vampire](/wiki/Skyrim:Vampire "Skyrim:Vampire") lair.
3. Report back to Gunmar.

## Detailed Walkthrough

Gunmar will inform you that he has discovered a vampire lair and will task you with eliminating its head vampire. While you only need to kill the boss vampire in order to scatter its minions, he heartily recommends you thoroughly cleanse the lair of all vampires and thralls. He will then mark a random [vampire lair](/wiki/Category:Skyrim-Places-Vampire_Lairs "Category:Skyrim-Places-Vampire Lairs") on your map.

Travel to the location and dispose of the vampire boss and other enemies. Once you are done, return to Gunmar for your reward: a leveled enchanted item.

## Bugs

- If the radiant system assigns [Movarth's Lair](/wiki/Skyrim:Movarth%27s_Lair "Skyrim:Movarth's Lair"), you will be unable to complete this quest as there is no standard boss set at that location.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 1.3.2, fixes this bug.

Notes

- Any text displayed in angle brackets (e.g., `<Alias=LocationHold>`) is dynamically set by the Radiant Quest system, and will be filled in with the appropriate word(s) when seen in game.
- Not all Journal Entries may appear in your journal; which entries appear and which entries do not depends on the manner in which the quest is done.
- Stages are not always in order of progress. This is usually the case with quests that have multiple possible outcomes or quests where certain tasks may be done in any order. Some stages may therefore repeat objectives seen in other stages.
- If an entry is marked as "Finishes Quest" it means the quest disappears from the Active Quest list, but you may still receive new entries for that quest.
- On the PC, it is possible to use the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to advance through the quest by entering `setstage DLC1RH02 stage`, where `stage` is the number of the stage you wish to complete. It is not possible to un-complete (i.e. go back) quest stages, but it is possible to clear all stages of the quest using `resetquest DLC1RH02`.

# Skyrim:Cleansing the Stones

## Overview

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| [SR-qico-Main 2.png](/wiki/File:SR-qico-Main_2.png) | **Use the [Bend Will](/wiki/Skyrim:Bend_Will "Skyrim:Bend Will") [shout](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Shouts "Skyrim:Dragon Shouts") to cleanse each of the remaining [All-Maker Stones](/wiki/Skyrim:All-Maker_Stones "Skyrim:All-Maker Stones").** |

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Quest Giver: | [Storn Crag-Strider](/wiki/Skyrim:Storn_Crag-Strider "Skyrim:Storn Crag-Strider") |
| Location(s): | [Beast](/wiki/Skyrim:Beast_Stone "Skyrim:Beast Stone"), [Earth](/wiki/Skyrim:Earth_Stone "Skyrim:Earth Stone"), [Sun](/wiki/Skyrim:Sun_Stone "Skyrim:Sun Stone"), and [Water Stones](/wiki/Skyrim:Water_Stone "Skyrim:Water Stone") |
| Reward: | Access to the powers of each stone as they are cleansed |
| ID: | DLC2MQ03B |
| Suggested Level: | 10 |
| --- | |
| |  |  |  | | --- | --- | --- | | **← Previous** [The Fate of the Skaal](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Fate_of_the_Skaal "Skyrim:The Fate of the Skaal") | **Concurrent** [The Path of Knowledge](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Path_of_Knowledge "Skyrim:The Path of Knowledge"), [The Gardener of Men](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Gardener_of_Men "Skyrim:The Gardener of Men") | **Next →** [At the Summit of Apocrypha](/wiki/Skyrim:At_the_Summit_of_Apocrypha "Skyrim:At the Summit of Apocrypha") | | |
| |  |  | | --- | --- | | ← Previous | [The Fate of the Skaal](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Fate_of_the_Skaal "Skyrim:The Fate of the Skaal") | | Concurrent | [The Path of Knowledge](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Path_of_Knowledge "Skyrim:The Path of Knowledge"), [The Gardener of Men](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Gardener_of_Men "Skyrim:The Gardener of Men") | | → Next | [At the Summit of Apocrypha](/wiki/Skyrim:At_the_Summit_of_Apocrypha "Skyrim:At the Summit of Apocrypha") | | |

The [Sun Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Sun_Stone "Skyrim:Sun Stone") being cleansed

## Quick Walkthrough

1. Use the [Bend Will](/wiki/Skyrim:Bend_Will "Skyrim:Bend Will") [shout](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Shouts "Skyrim:Dragon Shouts") to cleanse the [Beast Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Beast_Stone "Skyrim:Beast Stone").
2. Use the Bend Will shout to cleanse the [Earth Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Earth_Stone "Skyrim:Earth Stone").
3. Use the Bend Will shout to cleanse the [Sun Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Sun_Stone "Skyrim:Sun Stone").
4. Use the Bend Will shout to cleanse the [Water Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Water_Stone "Skyrim:Water Stone").

## Detailed Walkthrough

With the [Wind Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Wind_Stone "Skyrim:Wind Stone") cleansed, return to [Skaal Village](/wiki/Skyrim:Skaal_Village "Skyrim:Skaal Village") and tell [Storn Crag-Strider](/wiki/Skyrim:Storn_Crag-Strider "Skyrim:Storn Crag-Strider") the good news. He will suggest you to do the same for the remaining four stones of Solstheim. He doubts it will fully stop whatever [Miraak](/wiki/Skyrim:Miraak_(person) "Skyrim:Miraak (person)") is doing, but it may slow his progress. Your map will be updated and show you the location of your targets: [Beast Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Beast_Stone "Skyrim:Beast Stone"), [Earth Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Earth_Stone "Skyrim:Earth Stone"), [Sun Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Sun_Stone "Skyrim:Sun Stone"), and [Water Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Water_Stone "Skyrim:Water Stone").

### Beast Stone

The Beast Stone is southwest of Skaal Village; this is the nearest stone you may find. Two entranced [Rieklings](/wiki/Skyrim:Riekling "Skyrim:Riekling") are working there. A leveled [cultist](/wiki/Skyrim:Cultist "Skyrim:Cultist") is patrolling around the stone and monitoring the work of Miraak's poor slaves. The cultist will attack you on sight, so defeat your enemy and use the [Bend Will](/wiki/Skyrim:Bend_Will "Skyrim:Bend Will") shout to cleanse the stone. The structure around the stone will collapse and a leveled [lurker](/wiki/Skyrim:Lurker "Skyrim:Lurker") will raise from the water. The two Rieklings won't turn hostile to you. They will stay here for a short moment then return to their tribe at Thirsk Mead Hall.

### Sun Stone

Keep traveling south and you'll find the Sun Stone in the north of [Tel Mithryn](/wiki/Skyrim:Tel_Mithryn_(settlement) "Skyrim:Tel Mithryn (settlement)"). A group of [Reavers](/wiki/Skyrim:Reaver "Skyrim:Reaver") are focusing on their building. Shout at the stone and a leveled lurker will attack you. The fight will be much easier with the help of these Reavers. They won't attack you after the combat; they'll just wander around the stone and give you some generic, non-hostile responses. After you leave this area, they will be removed from the game.

### Earth Stone

Travel to [Raven Rock](/wiki/Skyrim:Raven_Rock "Skyrim:Raven Rock") and you should find the Earth Stone without much trouble. [Bralsa Drel](/wiki/Skyrim:Bralsa_Drel "Skyrim:Bralsa Drel"), [Rirns Llervu](/wiki/Skyrim:Rirns_Llervu "Skyrim:Rirns Llervu"), and three [Redoran guards](/wiki/Skyrim:Redoran_Guard "Skyrim:Redoran Guard") have lost themselves here, doing their work mindlessly. Cleanse the stone and two lurkers will appear this time. One is near the stone, the other one is near the coastline. The guards will try their best to give you a hand. Pay close attention to the safety of Bralsa as she gives a quest later on. They will return to the city soon after regaining their freedom.

### Water Stone

Walk along the west coast of Solstheim to find the Water Stone. The shrine at this stone is being worked on by a group of sailors, and a cultist is monitoring their work. The cultist will attack you without hesitation. Defeat your enemy and do the same to the stone. A leveled lurker will rise from the water and try to kill you. In addition, a low-level [dragon](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon "Skyrim:Dragon") will fly in from the west. If you haven't already triggered the Rieklings hidden in barrels to the southeast, they'll also arrive shortly, which can make for a chaotic battle. Fortunately, you don't need to guarantee the safety of every sailor. They will return to their boat docked in the bay once they are freed. After you leave this area, they will sail back to Skyrim with their ship.

## Notes

- Before you cleanse the stones, the entranced people working there will repeat the following texts mechanically: *"Here in his shrine.(Here in his temple.) That they have forgotten. Here do we toil. That we might remember. By night we reclaim.(Here we reclaim.) What by day was stolen.(What faithless minds have stolen.) Far from ourselves. He grows ever near to us. Our eyes once were blinded. Now through him do we see. Our hands once were idle. Now through them does he speak. And when the world shall listen. And when the world shall see. And when the world remembers. That world will cease to be."*
- If you activate the stones before cleansing them, you will be in an entranced state, and [Miraak](/wiki/Skyrim:Miraak "Skyrim:Miraak") will repeat the following texts mechanically: *"Here in my shrine. (Here in my temple.) That you have forgotten. Here do you toil. That you might remember. By night you reclaim. What faithless minds have stolen. Far from yourself. I grow ever near to you. Your eyes once were blinded. Now through me do you see. Your hands once were idle. Now through them do I speak. And when the world shall listen. And when the world shall see. And when the world remembers. That world will cease to be."*
- If you activate any of the stones before cleansing them, you will be put into the same state as the rest of the occupants. However, unlike everyone else, you can exert your will and break free from the trance.
- The entranced Rieklings around the Beast Stone will repeat some similar texts in their own language: *"Wafoo athaaaal. Bertiflik a goroowala. Hra woong aba. Tika twafaara filik. Wilberk tikflaaar. Yuchaaa tungar cha tiweki. Bura warag faaanig. Tiri fuklik taaar aburak."*
- More people and Rieklings would appear at Beast Stone, Sun Stone, and Earth Stone during the night.
- Before you cleanse the stones, if you talk to someone who only works on the stones at night, they will say "The Master calls." as a reference to [Miraak](/wiki/Skyrim:Miraak "Skyrim:Miraak") when they head to the designated stone each night. They will use the same quotes as the entranced people until morning.
- All stones will be marked as "clear" on the map once you cleanse them.
- The [Tree Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Tree_Stone "Skyrim:Tree Stone") is the only All-Maker Stone that is not cleansed by the end of this quest.
- This quest must be completed to finish [The Gardener of Men](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Gardener_of_Men "Skyrim:The Gardener of Men") and the rest of the expansion's main questline.
- Prior to completing this quest, there is a chance that you will wake up at one of the stones whenever you sleep outdoors or in a dwelling, as long as the selected stone is still tainted.
  - The first time you sleep in an appropriate location, this random selection is guaranteed to occur, and as long as the selected stone has not already been cleansed, you will awake there. Thereafter, there is a 33% chance that a stone will be randomly selected for this purpose.
  - The Water Stone is not included in the list of stones you can wake up at.
- Activating each stone after freeing them will give you the powers of [Conjure Werebear](/wiki/Skyrim:Conjure_Werebear "Skyrim:Conjure Werebear") (Beast Stone), [Bones of the Earth](/wiki/Skyrim:Bones_of_the_Earth "Skyrim:Bones of the Earth") (Earth Stone), [Waters of Life](/wiki/Skyrim:Waters_of_Life "Skyrim:Waters of Life") (Water Stone), and [Sun Flare](/wiki/Skyrim:Sun_Flare "Skyrim:Sun Flare") (Sun Stone) until you use them. You can activate them to get the powers at most once per day. The powers granted by the stones work underwater.
- You can cleanse the stones before the quest has started. If you cleanse all of them before getting the Dragonborn quest, Storn will send you to find Frea at the Tree Stone, instantly completing Dragonborn and starting [The Temple of Miraak](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Temple_of_Miraak "Skyrim:The Temple of Miraak").

## Bugs

- When attempting to use the [Bend Will](/wiki/Skyrim:Bend_Will "Skyrim:Bend Will") shout on a corrupted stone, you may lose the ability to interact with it, but the event will not start, causing the quest to become stuck.
  - Travel to the Wind Stone and acquire its power to get the quest working properly. Stones you've already tried to cleanse will spawn Lurkers as soon as you near them but the shrines will not explode.
  - Alternatively, simply leaving the cell and returning to it, or saving and reloading the saved game, may resolve the problem, with the Lurker(s) appearing and the quest updating after the fight.
- As many as three lurkers may appear (rare). One or two may be a significant distance from the stone after cleansing it. (Even out in the ocean or falling off a cliff).
- If [Reluctant Steward](/wiki/Skyrim:Reluctant_Steward "Skyrim:Reluctant Steward") is finished and the Sun Stone has been cleansed, [Drovas Relvi](/wiki/Skyrim:Drovas_Relvi "Skyrim:Drovas Relvi")'s sleep package will always be active, and therefore he will be found sleeping indefinitely in [Tel Mithryn Steward's House](/wiki/Skyrim:Tel_Mithryn_Steward%27s_House "Skyrim:Tel Mithryn Steward's House").
  -  The [Unofficial Dragonborn Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Dragonborn_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Dragonborn Patch"), version 1.0.5, fixes this bug.
- If Reluctant Steward is finished and the Sun Stone has been cleansed, Drovas Relvi's sleep package may still have him trying to sleep at the [Retching Netch](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Retching_Netch "Skyrim:The Retching Netch"), even though he won't work there anymore.
  - The [Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Special_Edition_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Special Edition Patch"), version 4.1.3, fixes this bug.

## Quest Stages

- The following empty quest stages were omitted from the table: 0, 10, 15, 20, 25, 30, 35, 40, 45.

Notes

- Any text displayed in angle brackets (e.g., `<Alias=LocationHold>`) is dynamically set by the Radiant Quest system, and will be filled in with the appropriate word(s) when seen in game.
- Not all Journal Entries may appear in your journal; which entries appear and which entries do not depends on the manner in which the quest is done.
- Stages are not always in order of progress. This is usually the case with quests that have multiple possible outcomes or quests where certain tasks may be done in any order. Some stages may therefore repeat objectives seen in other stages.
- If an entry is marked as "Finishes Quest" it means the quest disappears from the Active Quest list, but you may still receive new entries for that quest.
- On the PC, it is possible to use the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to advance through the quest by entering `setstage DLC2MQ03B stage`, where `stage` is the number of the stage you wish to complete. It is not possible to un-complete (i.e. go back) quest stages, but it is possible to clear all stages of the quest using `resetquest DLC2MQ03B`.

# Skyrim:Clear-Headed

## Overview

|  |  |

| |  |  | | --- | --- | | ← Previous | [In A Pinch](/wiki/Skyrim:In_A_Pinch "Skyrim:In A Pinch") | | → Next | [Heart of Gold](/wiki/Skyrim:Heart_of_Gold "Skyrim:Heart of Gold") | | |

Clear-Headed

## Quick Walkthrough

1. Obtain a [glassfish](/wiki/Skyrim:Glassfish "Skyrim:Glassfish") for [Zaria](/wiki/Skyrim:Zaria "Skyrim:Zaria") in [Falkreath](/wiki/Skyrim:Falkreath "Skyrim:Falkreath").
2. Read Zaria's [note](/wiki/Skyrim:Zaria%27s_Note_from_Jarl "Skyrim:Zaria's Note from Jarl") from the Jarl.
3. Give the [Disguised Invisibility Potion](/wiki/Skyrim:Disguised_Invisibility_Potion "Skyrim:Disguised Invisibility Potion") to the guard in the [Falkreath Barracks](/wiki/Skyrim:Falkreath_Barracks "Skyrim:Falkreath Barracks").
4. Return to Zaria.

## Detailed Walkthrough

This quest can be started after [In A Pinch](/wiki/Skyrim:In_A_Pinch "Skyrim:In A Pinch") by speaking to Viriya:

:   **Know of anyone in need of fishing work around Skyrim?**
:   *"You're headed to Falkreath. It's all in this note."*

She will then hand you a [bounty](/wiki/Skyrim:Bounty:_Glassfish "Skyrim:Bounty: Glassfish") for a glassfish for [Zaria](/wiki/Skyrim:Zaria "Skyrim:Zaria") in Falkreath. Once you obtain a glassfish, head to [Grave Concoctions](/wiki/Skyrim:Grave_Concoctions "Skyrim:Grave Concoctions") in Falkreath to speak to Zaria:

:   **Here's the glassfish you requested in your bounty.**
:   *"I'm grateful for your efforts. Here, take this."*

She will then give you 200 gold and a [note](/wiki/Skyrim:Zaria%27s_Note_from_Jarl "Skyrim:Zaria's Note from Jarl") from the Jarl.

:   **Thanks for the coin. And... a note from the Jarl?**
:   *"Maybe you can help me."*

The note from the Jarl states that a guard has been stealing skooma from the evidence chest, and that the Jarl would like for the guard to have an invisibility potion poured into an empty skooma bottle to scare the guard straight. Speak to Zaria to obtain the invisibility potion:

:   **I'll deliver the disguised potion in exchange for the Jarl's ring.**
:   *"Thank you. Here, this is for you."*
:   **I'll return when the deed is done. Hopefully he learns his lesson.**
:   *"Good luck out there."*

She will then hand you a [Disguised Invisibility Potion](/wiki/Skyrim:Disguised_Invisibility_Potion "Skyrim:Disguised Invisibility Potion"). You will then need to head to the [Falkreath Barracks](/wiki/Skyrim:Falkreath_Barracks "Skyrim:Falkreath Barracks") to talk to the guard where you will have two options:

:   **Seems like you don't have any trouble keeping the edge off while on duty.**
:   *"I beg your pardon, sir. I don't know what you're getting at, but whatever it is, it's not appreciated."*

    :   **Here, take this. My way of saying thanks.**
    :   *"I understand. Now let's pledge never to speak of this again."*

:   **Here's a bottle of skooma I found laying about. I trust you'll lock it away?**
:   *"Of course."*

Either option leads to you needing to follow the guard into the jail, you can then overhear him say:

:   *"Soon. I can almost taste it."*

He will then drink the potion, turn invisible and then shout:

:   *"Oh, no! By the Gods! This can't be happening! Gods help us!"*

As you exit the jail, the guard will become visible again and say:

:   *"I don't feel... right... I'm going to lay down... for awhile..."*

Head back to Zaria and speak to her:

:   **I don't think that guard will be using skooma any longer.**
:   *"Excellent. You've done us a great service. Here is your reward."*

You will then be rewarded with the [Ring of Surroundings](/wiki/Skyrim:Ring_of_Surroundings "Skyrim:Ring of Surroundings").

## Notes

- When the invisible guard reappears after a short amount of time his inventory can then be picked and the Disguised Invisibility Potion can be stolen back and kept.
- Killing the guard after he drinks the potion will still allow you to collect the reward from Viriya since the guard will not "be using skooma any longer." You will however almost certainly incur a bounty since other guards are nearby.

## Bugs

- The dialogue to speak to the guard may not appear. **?**
  - Attack the guard, then go to jail and serve your time. After this, speaking to the guard gives you the related dialogue.
- The note from the Jarl may remain a quest item after completion.

## Quest Stages

| Clear-Headed (ccBGSSSE001\_Misc\_Falkreath) | | |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Stage | Finishes Quest | Journal Entry |
| 0 |  | Zaria, the proprietor of Grave Concoctions in Falkreath, is in need of someone to bring her a glassfish for use in potion making. *Objective 0:* Obtain a glassfish for Zaria in Falkreath  *Objective 10:* Speak to Zaria |
| 20 |  | I gave Zaria the glassfish she requested. She handed me a sum of gold along with a note. I should read what the note has to say. *Objective 20:* Read Zaria's note from Jarl <Alias=Jarl> |
| 30 |  | Someone in the city guard may be using skooma, and the Jarl has asked for Zaria's help in stopping it. Zaria plans to brew an invisibility potion disguised as a bottle of skooma. I should give the bottle to the guard suspected of using skooma in the Falkreath Barracks. Now that I understand Zaria and the Jarl's plan, I should obtain the disguised potion from Zaria. *Objective 30:* Obtain the disguised invisibility potion from Zaria |
| 40 |  | Zaria gave me her invisibility potion disguised as a bottle of skooma. I should hand it over to the guard inside the barracks. *Objective 40:* Give the disguised invisibility potion to the guard in the Falkreath Barracks |
| 45 |  | I killed the guard suspected of using skooma in the Falkreath Barracks. I should let Zaria know. *Objective 61:* Tell Zaria that the guard is dead |
| 50 |  | I handed the invisibility potion disguised as skooma over to the guard inside the barracks. I should follow him to see if he tries to use the "skooma". *Objective 50:* Follow the guard into the Falkreath Barracks Jail |
| 70 |  | I watched as the guard drank the potion disguised as skooma. He seemed truly distraught after he saw himself turn invisible. Hopefully this is the last of his skooma using days. I should let Zaria know that the plan worked. *Objective 60:* Return to Zaria |
| 200 | ☑ | I let Zaria know that the plan to scare the guard away from using skooma was a success. She rewarded me with an enchanted ring from the Jarl himself. |
| 200 | ☑ | I let Zaria know that I killed the guard suspected of using skooma. She clearly disapproved of my methods, but still rewarded me with an enchanted ring from the Jarl nonetheless. |

- The following empty quest stages were omitted from the table: 60, 65, 75.

Notes

- Any text displayed in angle brackets (e.g., `<Alias=LocationHold>`) is dynamically set by the Radiant Quest system, and will be filled in with the appropriate word(s) when seen in game.
- Not all Journal Entries may appear in your journal; which entries appear and which entries do not depends on the manner in which the quest is done.
- Stages are not always in order of progress. This is usually the case with quests that have multiple possible outcomes or quests where certain tasks may be done in any order. Some stages may therefore repeat objectives seen in other stages.
- If an entry is marked as "Finishes Quest" it means the quest disappears from the Active Quest list, but you may still receive new entries for that quest.
- On the PC, it is possible to use the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to advance through the quest by entering `setstage ccBGSSSE001_Misc_Falkreath stage`, where `stage` is the number of the stage you wish to complete. It is not possible to un-complete (i.e. go back) quest stages, but it is possible to clear all stages of the quest using `resetquest ccBGSSSE001_Misc_Falkreath`.

# Skyrim:Clearpine Pond

## Overview

Clearpine Pond

**Clearpine Pond** is a pond with a small island, located west-southwest of [Solitude](/wiki/Skyrim:Solitude "Skyrim:Solitude"), just to the northeast of [Pinemoon Cave](/wiki/Skyrim:Pinemoon_Cave "Skyrim:Pinemoon Cave").

The island is easily identifiable by the pile of logs and multiple fallen trees surrounding the island.

## Clearpine Pond

The island is inhabited by from one to three [spriggans](/wiki/Skyrim:Spriggan "Skyrim:Spriggan"), but they do not attack unless you come within close proximity or take items from the dead [alchemist](/wiki/Skyrim:Alchemist "Skyrim:Alchemist") or open the chest on the island. The spriggans can be engaged on your own terms by placing a rune spell at the base of the trees they're hiding in, similar to the way you can flush out draugr and skeletons slumbering inside sarcophagi. The spriggans will not cross the water surrounding the island, so you can easily pick them off with ranged weapons or spells or retreat and heal yourself if you struggle in a melee fight with them.

The chest on the island has a novice-level lock and is located inside a large rotten tree stump. There is a dead alchemist leaning up against the remains of the fallen tree trunk. On her person is a copy of the [Alchemy](/wiki/Skyrim:Alchemy "Skyrim:Alchemy") [skill book](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Books "Skyrim:Skill Books") *[De Rerum Dirennis](/wiki/Skyrim:De_Rerum_Dirennis "Skyrim:De Rerum Dirennis")* and both on her person and in an apothecary's satchel beside her there are several alchemical [ingredients](/wiki/Skyrim:Ingredients "Skyrim:Ingredients"). The island has many harvestable plants and fungi growing on it and on the shore around the pond, as listed below, in addition to the three [taproots](/wiki/Skyrim:Taproot "Skyrim:Taproot") recoverable from the spriggans.

Harvestable ingredients:

- 9 [Blue Mountain Flowers](/wiki/Skyrim:Blue_Mountain_Flower "Skyrim:Blue Mountain Flower")
- 3 [Mora Tapinella](/wiki/Skyrim:Mora_Tapinella "Skyrim:Mora Tapinella")
- 5 [Purple Mountain Flowers](/wiki/Skyrim:Purple_Mountain_Flower "Skyrim:Purple Mountain Flower")
- 7 [Red Mountain Flowers](/wiki/Skyrim:Red_Mountain_Flower "Skyrim:Red Mountain Flower")
- 3 [Thistle Branches](/wiki/Skyrim:Thistle_Branch "Skyrim:Thistle Branch")

# Skyrim:Clearspring Cave

## Overview

|  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- |
| |  | | --- | | Cave: Clearspring Cave ([view on map](https://gamemap.uesp.net/sr/?world=Skyrim&centeron=Clearspring+Cave)) | | |

| Console Location Code(s) | |

| Location | |
| West of [Shor's Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Shor%27s_Stone "Skyrim:Shor's Stone") East of [Snapleg Cave](/wiki/Skyrim:Snapleg_Cave "Skyrim:Snapleg Cave") | |
| [Ore Veins](/wiki/Skyrim:Mining "Skyrim:Mining") | |
| # of [Iron](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Ore "Skyrim:Iron Ore") | 1 |

Clearspring Cave

**Clearspring Cave** is a small [cave](/wiki/Skyrim:Caves "Skyrim:Caves") west of [Shor's Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Shor%27s_Stone "Skyrim:Shor's Stone") containing a [troll](/wiki/Skyrim:Troll "Skyrim:Troll"). It contains only one zone, *[Clearspring Cave](#Clearspring_Cave)*.

The Bow of the Hunt and *Vernaccus and Bourlor*

### Exterior

The cave entrance is unmarked and easily missed. From [Clearspring Tarn](/wiki/Skyrim:Clearspring_Tarn "Skyrim:Clearspring Tarn"), move a few meters north toward the cliff edge (overlooking [Eastmarch](/wiki/Skyrim:Eastmarch "Skyrim:Eastmarch") to the north). Look down a few feet for the path that tracks across the cliff face. The cave is located at the right end of that path, and its entrance is a great place to enjoy a gorgeous view of Eastmarch.

### Clearspring Cave

The cave itself is located underneath the tarn, whose waters seep through the ceiling. The first half of the chamber is partially flooded with the water pooling on the left, with an [iron ore vein](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Ore_Vein "Skyrim:Iron Ore Vein") in front of the pool as you enter. Mushrooms can be found along the path from the entrance, and [hanging moss](/wiki/Skyrim:Hanging_Moss "Skyrim:Hanging Moss") is abundant and can be harvested around the edges overhanging the pool. There is a [skeleton](/wiki/Skyrim:Skeleton "Skyrim:Skeleton") floating in the water to the left of the bridge with a leveled one-handed [weapon](/wiki/Skyrim:Weapons "Skyrim:Weapons") and a random [shield](/wiki/Skyrim:Shield "Skyrim:Shield") at the bottom of the pool beneath him.

The second half of the chamber is slightly larger and full of various flora and fungi, as well as numerous bones, both human and animal. The sole occupant of the cave, a [troll](/wiki/Skyrim:Troll "Skyrim:Troll"), makes its home here. Toward the back of the chamber is an altar holding the unique [Bow of the Hunt](/wiki/Skyrim:Bow_of_the_Hunt "Skyrim:Bow of the Hunt") and a copy of the [Archery](/wiki/Skyrim:Archery "Skyrim:Archery") [skill book](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Books "Skyrim:Skill Books") *[Vernaccus and Bourlor](/wiki/Skyrim:Vernaccus_and_Bourlor "Skyrim:Vernaccus and Bourlor")*. To the right of this is an unlocked wooden [chest](/wiki/Skyrim:Chest "Skyrim:Chest"), with leveled [potions](/wiki/Skyrim:Potions "Skyrim:Potions") of [healing](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Healing "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Healing") and [magicka](/wiki/Skyrim:Potion_of_Minor_Magicka "Skyrim:Potion of Minor Magicka") in front. There is a second skeleton that can be looted just to the right of the troll's nest, and by the edge of the water, on the right after crossing the earthen bridge a random sword either found among various gory bones or hanging high overhead.

With the [Fishing](/wiki/Skyrim:Fishing "Skyrim:Fishing") [Creation](/wiki/Skyrim:Creation_Club "Skyrim:Creation Club") installed, three [tripod spiderfish](/wiki/Skyrim:Tripod_Spiderfish "Skyrim:Tripod Spiderfish") and a [direfish](/wiki/Skyrim:Direfish "Skyrim:Direfish") can be caught by hand in the ponds on either side of the causeway.

## Notes

- The guaranteed troll spawn makes this cave dangerous to low-level characters.
- The cave contains a large amount of alchemy [ingredients](/wiki/Skyrim:Ingredients "Skyrim:Ingredients") (including the [troll fat](/wiki/Skyrim:Troll_Fat "Skyrim:Troll Fat") from the troll's corpse).
- There is no separate map marker for the cave; however, Clearspring Tarn is marked as cleared once the troll is destroyed.

## Maps

- 

  Clearspring Cave

## Overview

Clearspring Tarn

**Clearspring Tarn** is a small mountain pool on the cliff overlooking [Eastmarch](/wiki/Skyrim:Eastmarch "Skyrim:Eastmarch"), due east of [Snapleg Cave](/wiki/Skyrim:Snapleg_Cave "Skyrim:Snapleg Cave") and west of [Shor's Stone](/wiki/Skyrim:Shor%27s_Stone "Skyrim:Shor's Stone").

## Related Quests

- **[Animal Extermination](/wiki/Skyrim:Animal_Extermination_(B) "Skyrim:Animal Extermination (B)")**: Fulfill a contract given to the [Companions](/wiki/Skyrim:Companions "Skyrim:Companions") to clear out a beast den. ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))
- **[Salty Sea-Dogs](/wiki/Skyrim:Salty_Sea-Dogs "Skyrim:Salty Sea-Dogs")**: Find some [void salts](/wiki/Skyrim:Fine-Cut_Void_Salts "Skyrim:Fine-Cut Void Salts") for an inexperienced [sea captain](/wiki/Skyrim:Captain_Wayfinder "Skyrim:Captain Wayfinder"). ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))
- **[A New Order](/wiki/Skyrim:A_New_Order "Skyrim:A New Order")**[DG](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard"): Recruit [Isran](/wiki/Skyrim:Isran "Skyrim:Isran")'s old allies for the [Dawnguard](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard_(faction) "Skyrim:Dawnguard (faction)"). ([radiant](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant "Skyrim:Radiant"))

- This location is one of many potential targets for [one or more of the Radiant quests](/wiki/Skyrim:Radiant#Quest_Locations "Skyrim:Radiant").

## Clearspring Tarn

Beyond its aesthetic beauty, the tarn is mostly a landmark for the location of the [Clearspring Cave](/wiki/Skyrim:Clearspring_Cave "Skyrim:Clearspring Cave") that is hidden beneath it. An apprentice-locked wooden [chest](/wiki/Skyrim:Chest "Skyrim:Chest") can be found in the water along with a surprising variety of small fish that can be caught for use in [alchemy](/wiki/Skyrim:Alchemy "Skyrim:Alchemy"). [Goldfish](/wiki/Skyrim:Goldfish "Skyrim:Goldfish") can also be found in the water.

You may encounter a pair of [hunters](/wiki/Skyrim:Hunter "Skyrim:Hunter") that are busy pursuing their quarry as there are a large number of elk in the region.

There is a small cave to the west of the tarn with a path heading northeast past the tarn, after a short way the path splits with the right fork leading back under the tarn to the entrance to Clearspring Cave and the left fork heading in the direction of [Darkwater Crossing](/wiki/Skyrim:Darkwater_Crossing "Skyrim:Darkwater Crossing").

To achieve "Cleared" status, kill the Troll in Clearspring Cave below.

# Skyrim:Cliffside Retreat

## Overview

|  |  |  |  |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| |  |  | | --- | --- | | [SR-mapicon-Shack.png](/wiki/File:SR-mapicon-Shack.png) | Shack: Cliffside Retreat ([view on map](https://gamemap.uesp.net/sr/?world=Skyrim&centeron=Cliffside+Retreat)) | | |

Cliffside Retreat

**Cliffside Retreat** is a small [shack](/wiki/Skyrim:Shacks "Skyrim:Shacks") south of [Dragon Bridge](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Bridge "Skyrim:Dragon Bridge").

The shack is inhabited by a lone bear [hunter](/wiki/Skyrim:Hunter "Skyrim:Hunter"), who spends all day sitting on the wooden ledge overlooking [Chillwind Depths](/wiki/Skyrim:Chillwind_Depths "Skyrim:Chillwind Depths") and does not sleep. The shack has a bed that is free to use.

## Residents

| Residents |
| --- |
| [Hunter](/wiki/Skyrim:Hunter "Skyrim:Hunter") |

## Related Quests

- **[Double-Edged](/wiki/Skyrim:Double-Edged "Skyrim:Double-Edged")**[CC](/wiki/Skyrim:Alternative_Armors_-_Leather "Skyrim:Alternative Armors - Leather"): Determine the fate of a Thalmor agent.

## Walkthrough

The small open shack contains an unowned bed with a set of shelves beside it. All the items in and around the shack and on the wooden platform are marked as owned, and taking them is considered stealing. The shelves hold a copy of the [Archery](/wiki/Skyrim:Archery "Skyrim:Archery") [skill book](/wiki/Skyrim:Skill_Books "Skyrim:Skill Books") *[The Marksmanship Lesson](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Marksmanship_Lesson "Skyrim:The Marksmanship Lesson")*, three [red apples](/wiki/Skyrim:Red_Apple "Skyrim:Red Apple"), two [carrots](/wiki/Skyrim:Carrot "Skyrim:Carrot"), and a [cabbage](/wiki/Skyrim:Cabbage "Skyrim:Cabbage"). Leaning against the foot of the bed are a leveled [bow](/wiki/Skyrim:Bow "Skyrim:Bow") and a quiver of [steel arrows](/wiki/Skyrim:Steel_Arrow "Skyrim:Steel Arrow"). The south wall of the hut is open with a deck attached. On the deck is a table with two [cave bear pelts](/wiki/Skyrim:Cave_Bear_Pelt "Skyrim:Cave Bear Pelt"), a [bear pelt](/wiki/Skyrim:Bear_Pelt "Skyrim:Bear Pelt"), and a [steel dagger](/wiki/Skyrim:Steel_Dagger "Skyrim:Steel Dagger") on it. Underneath the table are two [bear traps](/wiki/Skyrim:Bear_Trap "Skyrim:Bear Trap"), and by the corner of the shack is a respawning barrel of foodstuffs.

Behind the shack, to the north, is a [tanning rack](/wiki/Skyrim:Tanning_Rack "Skyrim:Tanning Rack"), while against the outside northeast wall is an open crate containing two more bear pelts and a cave bear pelt, with a set bear trap to the right. There is an unlit campfire a few paces east of the shack, near the wooden platform, where the [hunter](/wiki/Skyrim:Hunter "Skyrim:Hunter") sits. Beside him is an open-topped wooden box containing three red apples. There are several [lavender](/wiki/Skyrim:Lavender "Skyrim:Lavender") bushes around the site as well.

## Notes

- The only container in the area is the barrel, which [respawns](/wiki/Skyrim:Respawning "Skyrim:Respawning") and is therefore not safe to store items in.

# Skyrim:Climb the Steps

## Overview

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| **Deliver a load of goods up to [High Hrothgar](/wiki/Skyrim:High_Hrothgar "Skyrim:High Hrothgar") for [Klimmek](/wiki/Skyrim:Klimmek "Skyrim:Klimmek").** | |

|  |  |
| --- | --- |
| Quest Giver: | [Klimmek](/wiki/Skyrim:Klimmek "Skyrim:Klimmek") |
| Location(s): | [Ivarstead](/wiki/Skyrim:Ivarstead "Skyrim:Ivarstead"), [High Hrothgar](/wiki/Skyrim:High_Hrothgar "Skyrim:High Hrothgar") |
| Reward: | Leveled gold |
| [Disposition](/wiki/Skyrim:Disposition "Skyrim:Disposition"): | =1 ([Klimmek](/wiki/Skyrim:Klimmek "Skyrim:Klimmek")) |
| ID: | FreeformIvarstead04 |
| --- | |
| |  |  |  | | --- | --- | --- | |  | **Concurrent** [The Way of the Voice](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Way_of_the_Voice "Skyrim:The Way of the Voice") |  | | |
| |  |  | | --- | --- | | Concurrent | [The Way of the Voice](/wiki/Skyrim:The_Way_of_the_Voice "Skyrim:The Way of the Voice") | | |

The chest in front of the monastery

## Quick Walkthrough

1. Speak with Klimmek about his trips to [High Hrothgar](/wiki/Skyrim:High_Hrothgar "Skyrim:High Hrothgar").
2. Receive [Klimmek's Supplies](/wiki/Skyrim:Klimmek%27s_Supplies "Skyrim:Klimmek's Supplies"), and climb the steps to High Hrothgar.
3. Place supplies in indicated chest.
4. Return to Klimmek for your reward.

### Klimmek's Problem

*"I'm just not ready to make the climb to High Hrothgar."*

When you arrive in [Ivarstead](/wiki/Skyrim:Ivarstead "Skyrim:Ivarstead") for the first time, you will find [Klimmek](/wiki/Skyrim:Klimmek "Skyrim:Klimmek") and [Gwilin](/wiki/Skyrim:Gwilin "Skyrim:Gwilin") having a conversation on the bridge:

**Gwilin**: *"On your way up the 7,000 Steps again, Klimmek?"*
**Klimmek**: *"Not today. I'm just not ready to make the climb to High Hrothgar. The path isn't safe."*
**Gwilin**: *"Aren't the Greybeards expecting some supplies?"*
**Klimmek**: *"Honestly, I'm not certain. I've yet to be allowed into the monastery. Perhaps one day."*

Apparently Klimmek makes a trip every few weeks up the 7,000 steps to High Hrothgar to deliver supplies to the [Greybeards](/wiki/Lore:Greybeards "Lore:Greybeards"), though he has never actually seen them in person. Unfortunately, he is now older, and finds the climb more difficult. You can choose to help him, with the promise of a reward. He will give you a bag of supplies and ask you to place them in a chest outside the High Hrothgar monastery.

### Deliver the Goods

If you have already discovered High Hrothgar, you may simply travel there. If not, you must climb the 7,000 steps leading out of Ivarstead and up the mountainside, encountering some [wolves](/wiki/Skyrim:Wolf "Skyrim:Wolf") along the way. Once at the top of the 7,000 steps, you will see the monastery with a chest located in the center of a pair of stairwells that lead up to the building itself. Now just open the chest and place the supplies inside. Klimmek's supplies are found in the *Misc* section of the inventory.

### There and Back Again

Once you have placed the supplies in the chest, return to Klimmek, who will compensate you for your leg work. He will give you a level-dependent amount of gold as a reward.

| Levels | Reward |
| --- | --- |
| 1–9 | 500 |
| 10–19 | 750 |
| 20–29 | 1,000 |
| 30–39 | 1,250 |
| 40+ | 1,500 |

## Notes

- Klimmek's supplies will remain in the chest indefinitely. They can be taken and returned at any time, however doing so will not grant you any further reward. The supplies are also always persistent; placing them in the inventory of a corpse keeps them from despawning.
- There are only about 700 steps on the way up to High Hrothgar, not 7,000.
- Gwilin can sometimes be killed by nearby bears. In that case, Klimmek will no longer be on the bridge and you will have to track him down in order to start the quest.

## Bugs

- If you drop Klimmek's supplies after completing the quest, they will hover in the air and can be used as a platform of sorts.
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.5, fixes this bug.

## Quest Stages

| Climb the Steps (FreeformIvarstead04) | | |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Stage | Finishes Quest | Journal Entry |

| 200 | ☑ |  |
| *Unknown* |  | *Objective 20:* Return to Klimmek |

- The following empty quest stages were omitted from the table: 10, 250.

Notes

- Any text displayed in angle brackets (e.g., `<Alias=LocationHold>`) is dynamically set by the Radiant Quest system, and will be filled in with the appropriate word(s) when seen in game.
- Not all Journal Entries may appear in your journal; which entries appear and which entries do not depends on the manner in which the quest is done.
- Stages are not always in order of progress. This is usually the case with quests that have multiple possible outcomes or quests where certain tasks may be done in any order. Some stages may therefore repeat objectives seen in other stages.
- If an entry is marked as "Finishes Quest" it means the quest disappears from the Active Quest list, but you may still receive new entries for that quest.
- On the PC, it is possible to use the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to advance through the quest by entering `setstage FreeformIvarstead04 stage`, where `stage` is the number of the stage you wish to complete. It is not possible to un-complete (i.e. go back) quest stages, but it is possible to clear all stages of the quest using `resetquest FreeformIvarstead04`.

## Overview

Clinton Lylvieve

**Clinton Lylvieve** is a [Breton](/wiki/Skyrim:Breton "Skyrim:Breton") [child](/wiki/Skyrim:Child "Skyrim:Child") living in [Dragon Bridge](/wiki/Skyrim:Dragon_Bridge "Skyrim:Dragon Bridge"). He is the son of [Azzada](/wiki/Skyrim:Azzada_Lylvieve "Skyrim:Azzada Lylvieve") and [Michel](/wiki/Skyrim:Michel_Lylvieve "Skyrim:Michel Lylvieve"), and brother of [Julienne](/wiki/Skyrim:Julienne_Lylvieve "Skyrim:Julienne Lylvieve"). He wants to be a soldier, although he is too young, and spends most of his time "patrolling the town" accompanied by his pet [goat](/wiki/Skyrim:Goat "Skyrim:Goat") Lucky.

Clinton wears blue colored [child's clothes](/wiki/Skyrim:Child%27s_Clothes "Skyrim:Child's Clothes") and a pair of [shoes](/wiki/Skyrim:Clothing#000e80a8 "Skyrim:Clothing"), and is equipped with a simple [iron dagger](/wiki/Skyrim:Iron_Dagger "Skyrim:Iron Dagger"). He carries a [key](/wiki/Skyrim:Lylvieve_House_Key "Skyrim:Lylvieve House Key") to the [family's house](/wiki/Skyrim:Lylvieve_Family%27s_House "Skyrim:Lylvieve Family's House"), a selection of [food and toys](/wiki/Skyrim:Leveled_Lists#Child "Skyrim:Leveled Lists"), and a small amount of gold.

He wakes up at 8am and starts patrolling around the town for four hours. At midday, he returns home in order to eat lunch for two hours, before resuming his patrolling for another six hours. After this patrol he once again returns home for a two-hour dinner before heading to bed at 10pm.

## Related Quests

- **[Prophet (Dawnguard)](/wiki/Skyrim:Prophet_(Dawnguard) "Skyrim:Prophet (Dawnguard)")**[DG](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard"): Find and rescue [a Moth Priest](/wiki/Skyrim:Dexion_Evicus "Skyrim:Dexion Evicus") from the [vampires](/wiki/Skyrim:Volkihar_Vampire_Clan "Skyrim:Volkihar Vampire Clan").
- **[Prophet (Vampire)](/wiki/Skyrim:Prophet_(Vampire) "Skyrim:Prophet (Vampire)")**[DG](/wiki/Skyrim:Dawnguard "Skyrim:Dawnguard"): The time of prophecy has arrived! Locate [a Moth Priest](/wiki/Skyrim:Dexion_Evicus "Skyrim:Dexion Evicus") for the [vampires](/wiki/Skyrim:Volkihar_Vampire_Clan "Skyrim:Volkihar Vampire Clan").

### Prophet

If you ask him about the [Moth Priest](/wiki/Skyrim:Dexion_Evicus "Skyrim:Dexion Evicus") during the related quest, he will be excited to share the information with you:

:   *"I don't know what a Moth Priest is, but I did see an old man in a robe not long ago. He was riding in a wagon with some Imperial guards. They didn't stop to visit, though. They rode through town heading south, and went across the big bridge. It was only just a little bit ago. I bet you can catch them if you hurry up."*

## Dialogue

When approached he can say:

:   *"Are you a soldier? One day, I'm going to be a soldier!"*
:   *"Pa says I'm too young to fight in the [war](/wiki/Skyrim:Civil_War "Skyrim:Civil War"), but I can still help by patrolling the town."*
:   *"I wish I was a soldier! They get to travel and stay up late and have fun!"*
:   *"Have you met Lucky? He's my pet goat, and he helps me patrol the town."*

## Conversations

At home, Clinton might question his father about local woman [Olda](/wiki/Skyrim:Olda "Skyrim:Olda")'s odd relationship with the [brother](/wiki/Skyrim:Lodvar "Skyrim:Lodvar") of her [husband](/wiki/Skyrim:Horgeir "Skyrim:Horgeir"):

:   **Clinton:** *"Father, how come Olda's so mean to everyone? She's only ever happy when she's with Lodvar, and she's not even married to him!"*
:   **Azzada:** *"That's no business of yours, son. Mind you keep your nose out of it."*
:   **Clinton:** *"Fine."*

## Notes

- Although Clinton calls his pet goat Lucky in dialogue, the actual goat NPC doesn't have a name, instead just being labeled the generic "Goat".
  -  The [Unofficial Skyrim Patch](/wiki/Skyrim_Mod:Unofficial_Skyrim_Patch "Skyrim Mod:Unofficial Skyrim Patch"), version 2.0.4, fixes this bug.

# Skyrim:Coated in Blood

## Overview

| --- |

All users are welcome to make changes to the page. | **Bring a [Daedra heart](/wiki/Skyrim:Daedra_Heart "Skyrim:Daedra Heart") to [Moth gro-Bagol](/wiki/Skyrim:Moth_gro-Bagol "Skyrim:Moth gro-Bagol").** | |

Moth gro-Bagol cooling metal at his forge

## Quick Walkthrough

1. Speak to Moth gro-Bagol.
2. Return with a [Daedra heart](/wiki/Skyrim:Daedra_Heart "Skyrim:Daedra Heart").

## Detailed Walkthrough

Moth gro-Bagol has been ordered to make a special weapon for the [Jarl](/wiki/Skyrim:Jarl "Skyrim:Jarl") of [Markarth](/wiki/Skyrim:Markarth "Skyrim:Markarth"). To do so he needs to dip it in the blood of a [Daedra](/wiki/Skyrim:Daedra "Skyrim:Daedra"). All he needs is a heart though, and would appreciate it if you could bring him one.

He will give you a random base piece of armor in return.

## Notes

- This quest raises his [disposition](/wiki/Skyrim:Disposition "Skyrim:Disposition") towards you, allowing you to [marry](/wiki/Skyrim:Marriage "Skyrim:Marriage") him.

- If an entry is marked as "Finishes Quest" it means the quest disappears from the Active Quest list, but you may still receive new entries for that quest.
- On the PC, it is possible to use the [console](/wiki/Skyrim:Console "Skyrim:Console") to advance through the quest by entering `setstage FreeformMarkarthN stage`, where `stage` is the number of the stage you wish to complete. It is not possible to un-complete (i.e. go back) quest stages, but it is possible to clear all stages of the quest using `resetquest FreeformMarkarthN`.
